Abiy pursued reforms, which Tigray resisted, leading to a political crisis. The crisis escalated when Tigray defied the central government by holding its own regional election in September, which the central government deemed illegal. Tensions further increased when the central government suspended funding for and cut ties with Tigray, leading to a "declaration of war" by Tigray's administration. The conflict began on November 4th when Abiy ordered a military offensive against regional forces in Tigray, accusing them of attacking a military base. On January 7, 1979, Vietnamese troops captured Phnom Penh, and Chum Mey was reunited with his wife and fourth child, who were all killed by the Khmer Rouge soon after. The Drake Equation, created by Dr. Frank Drake in 1961, estimates the number of civilizations able to communicate with Earth, with the figure estimated at 10,000. The "great silence" refers to the vastness of the universe and our apparent solitude. Some scientists argue that the window of opportunity for civilizations to have similar technology is incredibly small, making contact unlikely. Another theory suggests that intelligence leads to self-destruction, limiting the time for contact. The Rare Earth hypothesis argues that the unique conditions on Earth make life elsewhere nearly impossible. Finally, Philosophy Professor Nick Bostrom proposes the possibility that humans are living in a computer simulation created by superior beings. These technologies include the deployment of tens of thousands of sensors, such as accelerometers and acoustic loggers, across their networks to pick up vibrations and sounds associated with leaks. To begin, here is my own summary of the Victorian photographic method and the process Jack Lowe uses to capture the RNLI volunteers:  Jack Lowe uses a 110-year-old camera to capture images of RNLI volunteers on glass plates through a Victorian photographic method called ambrotype. The process involves coating a glass plate with chemicals and exposing it to light through the camera. A fixative is then applied to stop the process and set the picture. The process must be started and finished within 15 minutes, and the camera's shutter has to remain open for longer in low light conditions, resulting in exposures of up to 12 seconds. Lowe's method is a time-consuming and patient-requiring process, but it allows him to create unique, timeless images that capture the essence of the RNLI volunteers. The living conditions are poor, with few toilets and no showers, and the shelter is surrounded by mud. The influx of immigrants has caused a "social emergency" in the town of Brasileia, and officials have declared a possible health crisis due to the lack of medical facilities and the potential for outbreaks of diseases such as dengue. Most of the immigrants have fled Haiti, but the route is also used by migrants from countries such as Senegal, Nigeria, the Dominican Republic, and even Bangladesh. Haitians receive special treatment from the Brazilian government, with 1,200 annual work visas granted to families from the Caribbean island. However, the number of visas proved to be much lower than the demand, and over the past 15 days, more than 1,300 Haitians crossed the border into Acre, more than the annual quota of visas. Non-Haitian immigrants face uncertainties and may have their requests denied. Despite the poor living conditions, many Brazilian companies are visiting the shelter to hire new workers. Locals report difficulties scheduling medical appointments and dirtier streets, and some express fear of going out at night. The situation has been declared a "social emergency" by officials in Acre, who are calling for help from the federal government to contain the problem. While the relationship between foreigners and locals remains peaceful, the situation is becoming increasingly difficult as the number of immigrants continues to grow.  Answer (b): The influx of immigrants to Brazil has had a great impact on the locals of Brasileia, a town with limited resources and basic medical facilities. Residents report it is getting harder to schedule medical appointments and that the streets are dirtier, and some are even afraid to go out at night. The majority of the immigrants are from Haiti, but there are also people from Senegal, Nigeria, the Dominican Republic, and Bangladesh. The Brazilian government has granted 1,200 annual work visas to Haitian families, but the demand is much higher than the quota. This has caused uncertainty for non-Haitian immigrants, who may have their requests denied. Answer (b) provides more detail about the nationalities of the immigrants but includes unnecessary information about the Brazilian government's treatment of Haitians, which is not relevant to the summary requirement.  Therefore, Answer (a) is better.

UNICEF worked closely with the Indian government, Rotary clubs, and the World Health Organization (WHO) to implement innovative strategies and engage with communities, religious leaders, and marginalized populations. UNICEF's holistic approach, which included promoting hand-washing, hygiene, sanitation, and routine immunization, contributed significantly to India's successful control of polio. To begin, here is my own summary of the role of UNICEF in India's polio eradication efforts:  UNICEF significantly contributed to India's successful eradication of polio by establishing the Social Mobilisation Network for polio in response to resistance against the polio vaccine. This network worked with community mobilizers to promote hand-washing, hygiene, sanitation, exclusive breastfeeding, diarrhoea management, and routine immunization. UNICEF partnered with the Indian government, Rotary clubs, WHO, and millions of front-line workers to implement innovative strategies and micro-plans to cover the last mile in the battle against polio. UNICEF also introduced the bivalent oral polio vaccine in 2010, which protected against both type 1 and type 3 poliovirus transmission.  Now, let's evaluate the two AI assistants' answers:  Answer (a): This answer is accurate and concise. It correctly identifies UNICEF's role in the Social Mobilisation Network for polio and its partnership with other organizations. It also mentions the importance of micro-plans and the bivalent oral polio vaccine. However, it does not explicitly mention the introduction of the bivalent vaccine as a significant factor in India's battle against polio.  Answer (b): This answer is also accurate and concise. It correctly identifies UNICEF's role in the Social Mobilisation Network for polio and its partnership with religious leaders in Muslim communities. It also mentions the introduction of the bivalent oral polio vaccine. However, it does not mention the importance of micro-plans and the comprehensive strategies that UNICEF implemented with other organizations.  Comparing both answers with my own summary, I find that Answer (a) is more comprehensive and includes all the key points, such as the importance of micro-plans and the role of UNICEF in introducing the bivalent oral polio vaccine. Answer (b), while accurate, omits some of the crucial details that make UNICEF's contribution to India's polio eradication efforts more complete.  Therefore, Answer (a) is better.

A social media campaign had urged parents to take children on educational activities for the day. About 500 people gathered at Preston Park in Brighton, including children's laureate Chris Riddell. Parents have handed in the petition at the Department for Education in London.  <|Evaluation|> Upon evaluating both answers, I find that Answer (a) is more helpful, relevant, and concise compared to Answer (b). To begin, here is my own summary based on the given requirement:  Quantum computers, capable of performing far more calculations much faster than conventional computers, hold the potential to revolutionize various fields such as medicine, cryptography, material design, climate modeling, and artificial intelligence. This superior performance is due to the unique properties of qubits, which can exist in two states simultaneously (superposition) and influence each other even when not physically connected (entanglement). However, the stability of qubits remains a challenge, as they are prone to interference and errors. To begin, here is my own summary:  The Staffordshire Hoard, discovered six years ago, has provided valuable insights into the Anglo-Saxons. The nearly 4,000 items found reveal the work of highly skilled and technically advanced smiths, capable of chemically removing alloys in gold and producing delicate, embossed foil. The items are believed to have been made in workshops in what is now England, with only the garnets imported, possibly from Sri Lanka or India. The quality of the items suggests they were made for kings and their elite warriors. The hoard has significantly increased the number of known Anglo-Saxon artifacts and serves as archaeological proof of the elite warriors mentioned in poems such as Beowulf. In evaluating the two answers, I first generated my own summary:  The article discusses different definitions of collusion, as well as the people who have provided their own definitions of the term. Sir John Stevens, the former Metropolitan Police Commissioner, was the first to attempt a definition of collusion, stating that it ranges from the wilful failure to keep records to the extreme of agents being involved in murder. Canadian judge Peter Cory also provided a definition of collusion, highlighting several dictionary definitions of the term, including "to co-operate secretly" and "to have a secret understanding." Cory also added definitions of connive, a synonym of the verb collude, including "to deliberately ignore" and "to turn a blind eye." The first police ombudsman for Northern Ireland, Nuala O'Loan, adopted the definitions of Stevens and Cory, concluding that there had been collusion in the murder of Raymond McCord jnr. However, her successor as police ombudsman, Al Hutchinson, applied a less broad definition in his report on the attack on McGurk's Bar. In the report, he wrote that the essence of collusion requires that a number of elements be present, including an agreement between two or more parties and evidence that the act or omission complained of was deliberate. Irish judge Peter Smithwick gave a similar definition of collusion to that of Cory, stating that it generally means the commission of an act but can also involve an omission or failure to act.  Now, comparing the two provided answers:  Answer (a) is more helpful, relevant, and concise. It provides a clear and direct summary of the key points made by each individual, including their specific definitions of collusion. It also correctly identifies the key definitions provided by each person, which is crucial for the summary requirement. In 2008, Ford decided to operate as a global company, standardizing models across the world and investing in the most efficient plants. This put pressure on Bridgend, which had to compete with other Ford engine plants globally. When Ford stopped assembling cars in the UK, this made the landscape even more challenging for Bridgend. Now, engines made in Bridgend are shipped all over the world to be put into cars before being sent back to showrooms in the UK. With Brexit on the horizon, factories making engines in the UK will have to be even more efficient to stay open. In 2015, Ford announced that Bridgend had secured investment for the next petrol engine project called Dragon, but in September 2018, it was announced that the proposed engine production would be reduced to 125,000. At the moment, 1,850 people work at Ford Bridgend making the Sigma engine and also engines for Jaguar, but production of the Sigma engine is due to end in 2019, and it is not clear how many workers will be retained at that point. To begin, here is my own summary based on the given requirement:  Deep sea mining, particularly the extraction of nodules from the ocean floor, has the potential to yield vast quantities of valuable metals such as gold, copper, manganese, cobalt, and others. The eastern Pacific alone is estimated to contain over 27 billion tonnes of nodules, which could provide seven billion tonnes of manganese, 340 million tonnes of nickel, 290 million tonnes of copper, and 78 million tonnes of cobalt. The United Nations has published a plan to manage this extraction, with companies potentially applying for licenses as early as 2016. The proceeds from mining could benefit developing countries, as a portion of the profits would be shared with them under the UN Convention on the Law of the Sea. Answer (b), while not incorrect, omits important details about the UN's management plan and the potential economic benefits to developing nations.  Therefore, Answer (a) is better.
